        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;

        }

          flex-wrap: no-wrap;

        }

        }

            width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





It seems Chrome ignores SameSite policy by sending protected cookies when: a request is intercepted by a service worker FetchEvent, then fired from within its context. As developers willingly opt to implement FetchEvent mainly for caching purposes, this behavior undermines CSRF protection expected from setting up SameSite attribute.



<span class="line"><!---->It seems Chrome ignores SameSite policy by sending protected cookies when: a request is intercepted by a service worker FetchEvent, then fired from within its context. As developers willingly opt to implement FetchEvent mainly for caching purposes, this behavior undermines CSRF protection expected from setting up SameSite attribute.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I've set up a simple demo page at 



<span class="line"><!---->I've set up a simple demo page at <!----></span>





https://prong-glory-novel.glitch.me



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://prong-glory-novel.glitch.me"><!---->https://prong-glory-novel.glitch.me<!----></a>





.



<span class="line"><!---->.<!----></span>





 The site responds with Set-Cookie the "None" "Lax" "Strict" cookies, then echos the Cookie header value in each response. Without a service worker registered, "cross-site page with a link back here" works as expected; "Lax" sent only for GET method, "Strict" not sent for neither GET nor POST. Once the worker registered however, the page will always show all three cookie values, indicating SameSite policy is not being enforced.



<span class="line"><!----> The site responds with Set-Cookie the "None" "Lax" "Strict" cookies, then echos the Cookie header value in each response. Without a service worker registered, "cross-site page with a link back here" works as expected; "Lax" sent only for GET method, "Strict" not sent for neither GET nor POST. Once the worker registered however, the page will always show all three cookie values, indicating SameSite policy is not being enforced.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





rfc6265bis 5.2.2.2. states two different scenarios for service workers: 1. Requests which simply pass through a Service Worker, 2. Requests which are initiated by the Service Worker itself. It seems Chrome handles the above case in the latter way, presumably because there is a direct call to fetch() is involved. However, I believe they should be handled in the former way; The worker cannot manipulate the Request object in any way, and all it can do with the object is to hand it over to the network or drop it. In my opinion, it is natural to think the request is actually originated from a top-navigation document, so it should be treated like so.



<span class="line"><!---->rfc6265bis 5.2.2.2. states two different scenarios for service workers: 1. Requests which simply pass through a Service Worker, 2. Requests which are initiated by the Service Worker itself. It seems Chrome handles the above case in the latter way, presumably because there is a direct call to fetch() is involved. However, I believe they should be handled in the former way; The worker cannot manipulate the Request object in any way, and all it can do with the object is to hand it over to the network or drop it. In my opinion, it is natural to think the request is actually originated from a top-navigation document, so it should be treated like so.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Cross-reported to Mozilla as Firefox exhibits the same behavior. Safari only sends "None" which I suppose is a different problem in itself.



<span class="line"><!---->Cross-reported to Mozilla as Firefox exhibits the same behavior. Safari only sends "None" which I suppose is a different problem in itself.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

I have no doubt if the request is created from within the worker in the background: i.e., fetch(new Request(...)), it should behave as-is. But it seems the disparity arises when, SameSite policy considers where each request is "originated" from, while the behavior in question only considers where one is "initiated" from: i.e., fetch(request).



<span class="line"><!---->I have no doubt if the request is created from within the worker in the background: i.e., fetch(new Request(...)), it should behave as-is. But it seems the disparity arises when, SameSite policy considers where each request is "originated" from, while the behavior in question only considers where one is "initiated" from: i.e., fetch(request).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FetchEvent is partially positioned as a network proxy in this case, often caching responses just like one. So it'd make sense if it'd behave like one transparently, and the current behavior in a sense "modifies" the original request. (Even though the internal logic probably does not work that way.)



<span class="line"><!---->FetchEvent is partially positioned as a network proxy in this case, often caching responses just like one. So it'd make sense if it'd behave like one transparently, and the current behavior in a sense "modifies" the original request. (Even though the internal logic probably does not work that way.)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This does imply some amendments to rfc6265bis 5.2.2.2. might be in order.



<span class="line"><!---->This does imply some amendments to rfc6265bis 5.2.2.2. might be in order.<!----></span>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/da0a6501cf321579bd46a27ff9fba1bb8ea910bb"><!---->https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/da0a6501cf321579bd46a27ff9fba1bb8ea910bb<!----></a>

commit 



<span class="line"><!---->commit <!----></span>





da0a6501cf321579bd46a27ff9fba1bb8ea910bb



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/da0a6501cf321579bd46a27ff9fba1bb8ea910bb"><!---->da0a6501cf321579bd46a27ff9fba1bb8ea910bb<!----></a>

Author: Ben Kelly <



<span class="line"><!---->Author: Ben Kelly &lt;<!----></span>





wanderview@chromium.org



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/wanderview@chromium.org"><!---->wanderview@chromium.org<!----></a>

<span class="line"><!---->&gt;<!----></span>

Date: Thu Oct 28 19:19:49 2021



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Thu Oct 28 19:19:49 2021<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fetch: Plumb request initiator through passthrough service workers.



<span class="line"><!---->Fetch: Plumb request initiator through passthrough service workers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL contains essentially two changes:



<span class="line"><!---->This CL contains essentially two changes:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. The request initiator origin is plumbed through service workers



<span class="line"><!---->1. The request initiator origin is plumbed through service workers<!----></span>



<br>





   that do `fetch(evt.request)`.  In addition to plumbing, this



<span class="line"><!---->   that do `fetch(evt.request)`.  In addition to plumbing, this<!----></span>



<br>





   requires changes to how we validate navigation requests in the



<span class="line"><!---->   requires changes to how we validate navigation requests in the<!----></span>



<br>





   CorsURLLoaderFactory.



<span class="line"><!---->   CorsURLLoaderFactory.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Tracks the original destination of a request passed through a



<span class="line"><!---->2. Tracks the original destination of a request passed through a<!----></span>



<br>





   service worker.  This is then used in the network service to force



<span class="line"><!---->   service worker.  This is then used in the network service to force<!----></span>



<br>





   SameSite=Lax cookies to treat the request as a main frame navigation



<span class="line"><!---->   SameSite=Lax cookies to treat the request as a main frame navigation<!----></span>

   where appropriate.

Date: Tue Nov 09 15:48:30 2021



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Tue Nov 09 15:48:30 2021<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fetch: Plumb navigation redirect chain through service workers



<span class="line"><!---->Fetch: Plumb navigation redirect chain through service workers<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Navigation redirection works differently than normal redirection.



<span class="line"><!---->Navigation redirection works differently than normal redirection.<!----></span>



<br>





Navigation requests are made using "manual" redirect mode which means



<span class="line"><!---->Navigation requests are made using "manual" redirect mode which means<!----></span>



<br>





the redirect is not immediately followed.  Instead the redirect location



<span class="line"><!---->the redirect is not immediately followed.  Instead the redirect location<!----></span>



<br>





is handed back up to the NavigationURLLoaderImpl which then manually



<span class="line"><!---->is handed back up to the NavigationURLLoaderImpl which then manually<!----></span>



<br>





follows the redirect.  This results in a new request being sent for each



<span class="line"><!---->follows the redirect.  This results in a new request being sent for each<!----></span>



<br>





step in the redirect chain.



<span class="line"><!---->step in the redirect chain.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL plumbs the redirect chain information from



<span class="line"><!---->This CL plumbs the redirect chain information from<!----></span>



<br>





NavigationURLLoaderImpl down through each request so it can be included



<span class="line"><!---->NavigationURLLoaderImpl down through each request so it can be included<!----></span>



<br>





with requests proxied by a passthrough service worker.



<span class="line"><!---->with requests proxied by a passthrough service worker.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For more detailed information about these changes please see the



<span class="line"><!---->For more detailed information about these changes please see the<!----></span>



<br>





internal design doc at:



<span class="line"><!---->internal design doc at:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://docs.google.com/document/d/1KZscujuV7bCFEnzJW-0DaCPU-I40RJimQKoCcI0umTQ/edit?usp=sharing



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1KZscujuV7bCFEnzJW-0DaCPU-I40RJimQKoCcI0umTQ/edit?usp=sharing"><!---->https://docs.google.com/document/d/1KZscujuV7bCFEnzJW-0DaCPU-I40RJimQKoCcI0umTQ/edit?usp=sharing<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





We have rough consensus to make this change in this spec issue:



<span class="line"><!---->We have rough consensus to make this change in this spec issue:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/issues/1335



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/issues/1335"><!---->https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/issues/1335<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





Note, this CL includes some expected test failures.  These are due to



<span class="line"><!---->Note, this CL includes some expected test failures.  These are due to<!----></span>



<br>





the "lax-allowing-unsafe" intervention that is currently enabled.  See:



<span class="line"><!---->the "lax-allowing-unsafe" intervention that is currently enabled.  See:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/web_tests/TestExpectations;l=4635;drc=e8133cbf2469adb99c6610483ab78bcfb8cc4c76



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/web_tests/TestExpectations;l=4635;drc=e8133cbf2469adb99c6610483ab78bcfb8cc4c76"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/web_tests/TestExpectations;l=4635;drc=e8133cbf2469adb99c6610483ab78bcfb8cc4c76<!----></a>



<br>



<br>

After working on the tests some more I have come to the conclusion we don't need any more code changes in this bug.  There are still some places where we incorrectly send SameSite cookies from service workers, but those require storage partitioning to fix.  That work is underway and will ship separately.



<span class="line"><!---->After working on the tests some more I have come to the conclusion we don't need any more code changes in this bug.  There are still some places where we incorrectly send SameSite cookies from service workers, but those require storage partitioning to fix.  That work is underway and will ship separately.<!----></span>

Keeping this open until I get review and confirmation of my understanding in the tests.



<span class="line"><!---->Keeping this open until I get review and confirmation of my understanding in the tests.<!----></span>

Add WPT tests for SameSite cookies in ServiceWorkers with nested frames.



<span class="line"><!---->Add WPT tests for SameSite cookies in ServiceWorkers with nested frames.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL adds a number of new cases to the service worker SameSite



<span class="line"><!---->This CL adds a number of new cases to the service worker SameSite<!----></span>



<br>





cookies test.  The cases break down into two general types:



<span class="line"><!---->cookies test.  The cases break down into two general types:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Cases where A1 frames B frames A2, and then A2 calls window.open()



<span class="line"><!---->1. Cases where A1 frames B frames A2, and then A2 calls window.open()<!----></span>



<br>





   to an A origin URL.



<span class="line"><!---->   to an A origin URL.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Cases where A1 frames B frames A2, and then A2 sets the location



<span class="line"><!---->2. Cases where A1 frames B frames A2, and then A2 sets the location<!----></span>



<br>





   to an A origin URL.



<span class="line"><!---->   to an A origin URL.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For (1) we expect SameSite strict cookies to be sent because



<span class="line"><!---->For (1) we expect SameSite strict cookies to be sent because<!----></span>



<br>





window.open() creates a top-level context that will have a populated



<span class="line"><!---->window.open() creates a top-level context that will have a populated<!----></span>



<br>





site-for-cookies and the initiator is same-origin (regardless of the



<span class="line"><!---->site-for-cookies and the initiator is same-origin (regardless of the<!----></span>



<br>





cross-site ancestor chain).



<span class="line"><!---->cross-site ancestor chain).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For (2) we expect only SameSite=None cookies to be sent.  This is



<span class="line"><!---->For (2) we expect only SameSite=None cookies to be sent.  This is<!----></span>



<br>





because setting the location results in a navigation to an A1->B->A3



<span class="line"><!---->because setting the location results in a navigation to an A1-&gt;B-&gt;A3<!----></span>



<br>





nested frame with an empty site-for-cookies.



<span class="line"><!---->nested frame with an empty site-for-cookies.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We currently fail the passthrough and change-request cases for (2).



<span class="line"><!---->We currently fail the passthrough and change-request cases for (2).<!----></span>



<br>





We plan to fix this as part of storage partitioning with an ancestor



<span class="line"><!---->We plan to fix this as part of storage partitioning with an ancestor<!----></span>



<br>





chain bit in the StorageKey.  See:



<span class="line"><!---->chain bit in the StorageKey.  See:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://github.com/privacycg/storage-partitioning/issues/25



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/privacycg/storage-partitioning/issues/25"><!---->https://github.com/privacycg/storage-partitioning/issues/25<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





This CL also includes some minor cleanup of the WPT test and associated



<span class="line"><!---->This CL also includes some minor cleanup of the WPT test and associated<!----></span>



<br>





resources.



<span class="line"><!---->resources.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

          position: absolute;

          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
